24:I[78891,["529","static/chunks/529-b3a318fab494e03f.js","244","static/chunks/244-f8e89f92ed6eb924.js","839","static/chunks/839-b514104c7e948606.js","165","static/chunks/165-ae3b45f0d86ef78d.js","184","static/chunks/app/dashboard/roots/%5Broot%5D/page-e0a9e2c37c8cb20d.js"],"CardTitle"]
25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. Be mindful of God, and He will teach you: He has full knowledge of everything26:T3567,<entryFree id="n38170" key="لَيْسَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">لَيْسَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> a word denoting negation: (S, A, K:) it is a verb in the pret. tense, (S, A, K, Mughnee,) having no other tense, (Sb, S, M, Msb, Mughnee,) nor a part. n. nor an inf. n.; (Sb, M, Msb; *) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِلَ</foreign>; (Mughnee;) originally <foreign lang="ar">لَيِسَ</foreign>, from which it is contracted by the suppression of a vowel, (Sb, * S, M, * K, Mughnee, *) being found difficult of pronunciation, (S,) [i. e.,] to render it easy to pronounce, (K,) like <foreign lang="ar">عَلْمَ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">عَلِمَ</foreign>, (Sb, M,) the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> not being changed into <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> (Sb, S, M) because it is imperfectly inflected, being used in the pret. form for the present, (S,) [i. e.,] because it has no future, nor part. n., nor inf. n., nor derivation, wherefore, not being perfectly inflected like its coordinates, it is made like that which is not a verb, as <foreign lang="ar">لَيْتَ</foreign>: (Sb, M:) what shows it to be a verb, (S, Mughnee,) not a particle occupying the place of <foreign lang="ar">مَا</foreign>, as Ibn-Es-Sarráj and some others after him have asserted, (Mughnee,) though not perfectly inflected like [other] verbs, (S,) is their saying <foreign lang="ar">لَسْتَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَسْتُمَا</foreign> (S, Mughnee) and <foreign lang="ar">لَسْتُمْ</foreign> (S) and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسُوا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَتْ</foreign> [&amp;c.], (Mughnee,) like as they say <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتُمَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتُمْ</foreign> [&amp;c.]: (S:) we have not determined its measure to be <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَ</foreign>, because this is not contracted; nor <foreign lang="ar">فَعُلَ</foreign>, because there is no verb of this measure with <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> for its medial radical letter, except <foreign lang="ar">هَيُؤَ</foreign>; but <foreign lang="ar">لُسْتَ</foreign> has been heard; so, accord. to this form, it may be like <foreign lang="ar">هَيُؤَ</foreign>: (Mughnee:) the Benoo-Dabbeh say <foreign lang="ar">لُسْتُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لُسْنَا</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">لَسْتُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَسْنَا</foreign>; and some of them say <foreign lang="ar">لِسْتُ</foreign>: (TA, art. <foreign lang="ar">لوس</foreign>:) but Sb says, that the Arabs did not say <foreign lang="ar">لِسْتَ</foreign>, like as they said <foreign lang="ar">خِفْتَ</foreign>, because <foreign lang="ar">ليس</foreign> is not perfectly inflected like [other] verbs. (M.) [There is also another opinion respecting its origin, which will be mentioned in the course of this article.] It [is generally a particular (not a universal) negative, and] denotes the negation of a thing at the present time; (M, Mughnee;) [i. e.] it denotes [thus] the negation of its predicate: (Msb:) and has the same government as the verb<foreign lang="ar">كَانَ</foreign> and its coordinates; (S;) governing the subject in the nom., and the predicate in the accus.: (S, Mughnee:) as when you say, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ زَيْدٌ قَائِمًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Zeyd is not a person standing</hi>]: (Msb:) and by means of the context, it denotes the negation of a thing at a time not the present; as in the saying of El-Aashà [respecting Mohammad], <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَهُ نَافِلَاتٌ مَا يُغِبُّ نَوَالُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَلَيْسَ عَطَآءُ اليَوْمِ مَانِعَهُ غَدَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">He has bounties the bestowing of which is not on alternate days; and the giving of to-day will not be a preventer of it to-morrow</hi>]; and [sometimes when it is followed by a verb, as] in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ خَلَقَ ٱللّٰهُ مِثْلَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">God has not created the like of him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi>] (Mughnee.) But it differs from its coordinates in that the prep. <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> may be prefixed to its predicate: as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ زَيْدٌ بِمُنْطَلِقٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Zeyd is not going away</hi>]; the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> being a means of the verb's being trans., and also corroborative of the negation: and one may optionally not introduce it, because one may do without the corroborative, and because some verbs are trans. sometimes by means of a prep. and sometimes without a prep., as <foreign lang="ar">اِشْتَقْتُكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِشْتَقْتُ إِلَيْكَ</foreign>. (S.) It also differs from its coordinates in that its predicate may not be put before it: for you may say <foreign lang="ar">مُحْسِنًا كَانَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ</foreign>, but not <foreign lang="ar">مُحْسِنًا لَيْسَ زَيْدٌ</foreign>: (S:) or some allow this latter; but others disallow it. (Ibn- 'Akeel on the Alfeeyeh, section on <foreign lang="ar">كان</foreign> and its coordinates.) It is also used as an exceptive particle, (S, M, Mughnee,) in the place of <foreign lang="ar">إِلَّا</foreign>; (S, Mughnee;) in which case [also] its subject [which is understood] is in the nom. case, and its predicate in the accus.: (S:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَنِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">القَوْمُ لَيْسَ زَيْدًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The company of men came to me, except Zeyd</hi>]; as though you said, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ الجَائِى</foreign> 
                  <pb n="2685"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدًا</foreign>. (S, M: but in the latter, instead of <foreign lang="ar">جاءنى</foreign>, we find <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى</foreign>; and instead of <foreign lang="ar">الجائى</foreign>, we find <foreign lang="ar">الآتِى</foreign>.) You may also say, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَنِى القَوْمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The company of men came to me, excepting thee</hi>]; but the separate pronoun, <foreign lang="ar">إِيَّاكَ</foreign>, is here better. (S.) When the predicate after it is connected with <foreign lang="ar">إِلَّا</foreign>, as in the ex. here next following, Benoo-Temeem make it in the nom. case: thus they say, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ الطِّيبُ إِلَّا المِسْكُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It is not perfume, except musk;</hi> meaning, nothing is perfume except musk]: which has been resolved is several ways; some holding <foreign lang="ar">الطيب</foreign> to be the subject of <foreign lang="ar">ليس</foreign>: but its being peculiar to the dial. of Temeem refutes the explanations here referred to: some, again, hold <foreign lang="ar">ليس</foreign> to be here used as a particle; and so in the saying <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ خَلَقَ ٱللّٰهُ مِثْلَهُ</foreign>, mentioned above. (Mughnee.) Sometimes it is used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">لَا التَّبْرِئَةِ</foreign> [the <foreign lang="ar">لا</foreign> which denies in a general manner to the uttermost, i. e., universally, or totally]; as is said in the K, except that in all the copies thereof we find <foreign lang="ar">وَإِنَّمَا</foreign> put by mistake for <foreign lang="ar">وَرُبَّمَا</foreign>: (TA:) [so in the saying in the Kur, ii. 194, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ</foreign>, which is the same as <foreign lang="ar">لَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ</foreign> in verse 235 of the same chapter, meaning, <hi rend="ital">There shall be no crime,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sin, chargeable upon you</hi>]. Sometimes, also, it is used as a connective particle, (Mughnee,) in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">لا</foreign> so used: (TA:) as in the saying [of a poet], <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَيْنَ المَفَرُّ وَالإِلٰهُ الغَالِبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَالأَشْرَمُ المَغْلُوبُ لَيْسَ الغَالِبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Where is the place of flight when God is the pursuer, and El-Ashram</hi> (meaning Abrahah) <hi rend="ital">is the overcome, not the overcomer?</hi>]: which has been resolved by supposing <foreign lang="ar">الغالب</foreign> to be the subject of <foreign lang="ar">ليس</foreign>, and the predicate to be suppressed; the latter being said by Ibn-Málik to be an annexed pronoun referring to El-Ashram; so that the meaning is <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَهُ الغَالِبُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the overcomer is not he</hi>]. (Mughnee.) It is said (M, K) by Fr, (M,) and also by Kh, (TA,) that the original of <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَيْسَ</foreign>; (M, K [in the latter of which I read <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ أَصْلُهُ</foreign>, as in several copies of the K, or rather <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ أَصْلُهَا</foreign>, as corrected in the TA, instead of <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ مَعْنَاهُ</foreign>, the reading in the CK];) and this, says Fr, is shown by the saying, <foreign lang="ar">جِئْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ مِنْ أَيْسَ وَلَيْسَ</foreign>, i. e., [<hi rend="ital">Bring thou him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">from where he,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is, and is not:</hi> (M:) or <foreign lang="ar">اِيتِنِى مِنْ حَيْثُ أَيْسَ وَلَيْسَ</foreign> i. e., [<hi rend="ital">Come thou to me,</hi> or probably, the right reading is <foreign lang="ar">اِيتِنِى بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">bring thou to me him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it,</hi> (as I find in a copy of the K, in which <foreign lang="ar">به</foreign> has been added in red ink, and in the A I find <foreign lang="ar">إِيتِ بِهِ</foreign>,)] <hi rend="ital">from where he,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is, and he,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is not:</hi> (K:) or the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">مِنع حَيْثُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَا وُجْدَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from where there is no finding;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">no being found,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">no existence;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">no power,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ability</hi>]: (K, * TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">أَيْسَ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">مَوْجُودٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">found,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">existing</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَيْسَ</foreign> [means] <foreign lang="ar">لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَوْجُودٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">not found,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">not existing</hi>], and is contracted [into <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ</foreign>]: (K:) [but the last rendering of <foreign lang="ar">ايس</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لا ايس</foreign> seems to be taken from an explanation, not literal, of another saying; <foreign lang="ar">مَا يَعْرِفُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَيْسَ مِنْ لَيْسَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">he knows not a thing existing from a thing not existing.</hi>] Aboo-'Alee relates, that Sb said, <foreign lang="ar">جِئْ بِهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ وَلَيْسَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Bring thou him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, from where he,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is and is not</hi>]; meaning, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَيْسَ</foreign>, the fet-hah of the <foreign lang="ar">س</foreign> being made full in sound, on account of the pause. (M.) In the saying of a certain poet, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ رُسَّتِ الحَاجَاتُ عِنْدَ قَيْسِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذْ لَا يَزَالُ مُولَعًا بِلَيْسِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Wants have been forgotten as old things</hi> (so <foreign lang="ar">رُسَّت</foreign> is explained in the M, as used here, in art. <foreign lang="ar">رس</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">with Keys, since he ceases not to be addicted to</hi> the use of <hi rend="ital">the word leysa</hi>], it is made by him a noun, and declined.
